- [ ] I want to talk about unpaid leave a little bit because sometimes that's where we have some issues. So for exempt employees, unpaid leave must be taken in full-day increments unless it is coded as family medical leave. That's something that not everybody knows, so it has to be a full day if somebody's taking unpaid. Another thing that is not also always known is staff need to use all paid options before using unpaid. So an employee would need to use all their vacation, all their paid leave, including holiday, before they were to use unpaid leave. The only exception would be for an approved family medical leave. 5 or more occurrences of unpaid time need to be reported to me. So if you have somebody that is out for 5 days unpaid, just let me know. We just talked about it. A tip, so you don't want to get to the end of the business quarter, employee and have unpaid time or hours that you're not sure where they're going to go to. So I always recommend that employees put something in their time card so that they don't get to the end of the business quarter and end up in a bad situation. So an example would be, okay, I was sick a couple of weeks ago, and so I put paid leave in my time card by I work extra later on, I'll go back and change it. It's not, oh, I plan to make up the time and just leave it blank. We always want to have something reported so that we don't have anybody get into that scenario. I'm sure Carol will talk about this a little bit more, but if you do have an employee charged to unpaid, it's going to come out of their salary. Um, a prose linter specifically is made to go through a text that's meant to be read in a web interface, or it could be read in a local interface too, but it's meant to be read and it checks for things that you tell it to, like it could check against AP style, it could check for lab-specific style guide things that we want to make sure that we go by, it can check for passive voice, it can check for things like are the acronyms spelled out, are we Are we talking about our acronyms correctly?
